      "body": "### Summary\r\n\r\nCurrently a ansible collection within the folder specified with `collections_paths` does NOT take priority over `site-packages/ansible_collections` resulting in older collections from that path overwriting newer git checkouts from within the playbooks directory.\r\n`ansible-galaxy collection list` will show both with the one from the `collections_path` first. But when `ansible-galaxy collection verify` is ran it'll show only the one from site-packages. Also ansible won't use the newer version from the `collections_paths` directory.\r\n\r\nEither ansible should use the newest version from any of the configured locations or the collections_paths one should always overwrite the bundled one from site-packages. But defaulting to always using the one from site-packages is not just non-intuitive, but it also causes issues with people trying to upgrade to a newer version of the collection because of a bug or just trying to pin one for a deterministic run that doesn't break because of newly introduced bugs.\r\n\r\nNote: could be that this only happens when a collections_path is shared between multiple playbooks. I didn't try to freshly install the collection with galaxy into each one. I've configured the `collections_paths` setting within my playbooks to point to a centralized location with the versions I'd like ansible to use.\r\n\r\n### Issue Type\r\n\r\nBug Report\r\n\r\n### Component Name\r\n\r\ncollections\r\n\r\n### Ansible Version\r\n\r\n```console\r\n$ ansible --version\r\nansible [core 2.15.5]\r\n  config file = /home/user/git/project001/ansible.cfg\r\n  configured module search path = ['/home/user/.ansible/plugins/modules', '/usr/share/ansible/plugins/modules']\r\n  ansible python module location = /home/user/git/project001/venv/lib/python3.12/site-packages/ansible\r\n  ansible collection location = /home/user/git/my_ansible_collections\r\n  executable location = /home/user/git/project001/venv/bin/ansible\r\n  python version = 3.12.0 (main, Oct 21 2023, 18:43:16) [GCC 13.2.1 20230801] (/home/user/git/project001/venv/bin/python)\r\n  jinja version = 3.1.2\r\n  libyaml = False\r\n```\r\n\r\n\r\n### Configuration\r\n\r\n```console\r\n# if using a version older than ansible-core 2.12 you should omit the '-t all'\r\n$ ansible-config dump --only-changed -t all\r\nCOLLECTIONS_PATHS(/home/user/git/project001/ansible.cfg) = ['/home/user/git/my_ansible_collections']\r\nCONFIG_FILE() = /home/user/git/project001/ansible.cfg\r\nDEFAULT_BECOME(/home/user/git/project001/ansible.cfg) = True\r\nDEFAULT_FORCE_HANDLERS(/home/user/git/project001/ansible.cfg) = True\r\nDEFAULT_FORKS(/home/user/git/project001/ansible.cfg) = 50\r\nDEFAULT_MANAGED_STR(/home/user/git/project001/ansible.cfg) = This file is managed by ansible - local changes will be lost\r\nDEFAULT_REMOTE_USER(/home/user/git/project001/ansible.cfg) = root\r\nDEFAULT_TRANSPORT(/home/user/git/project001/ansible.cfg) = ssh\r\nDEFAULT_VAULT_PASSWORD_FILE(/home/user/git/project001/ansible.cfg) = /home/user/git/project001/.vpass\r\nDEPRECATION_WARNINGS(/home/user/git/project001/ansible.cfg) = True\r\nRETRY_FILES_ENABLED(/home/user/git/project001/ansible.cfg) = True\r\nSYSTEM_WARNINGS(/home/user/git/project001/ansible.cfg) = True\r\n\r\nCONNECTION:\r\n==========\r\n\r\nparamiko_ssh:\r\n____________\r\nremote_user(/home/user/git/project001/ansible.cfg) = root\r\nssh_args(/home/user/git/project001/ansible.cfg) = -o ForwardAgent=no -o UserKnownHostsFile=known_hosts -o ControlMaster=auto -o ControlPersist=60s -o PreferredAuthentications=publickey -o ServerAliveInterval=11\r\n\r\nssh:\r\n___\r\npipelining(/home/user/git/project001/ansible.cfg) = True\r\nremote_user(/home/user/git/project001/ansible.cfg) = root\r\nssh_args(/home/user/git/project001/ansible.cfg) = -o ForwardAgent=no -o UserKnownHostsFile=known_hosts -o ControlMaster=auto -o ControlPersist=60s -o PreferredAuthentications=publickey -o ServerAliveInterval=11\r\n```\r\n\r\n\r\n### OS / Environment\r\n\r\nArchLinux with ansible within venv\r\n\r\n### Steps to Reproduce\r\n\r\n<!--- Paste example playbooks or commands between quotes below -->\r\n1. Add a collection that is also bundled with ansible into the collections folder, like \"community.docker\"\r\n2. Use ansible-galaxy to check the collections that are detected\r\n```\r\nansible-galaxy collection list\r\n# lists community.docker twice, first for our configured folder and a 2nd time for the one shipped with ansible\r\nansible-galaxy collection verify\r\n# only shows the one that shipped with ansible, ignoring ours.\r\n```\r\n\r\n\r\n### Expected Results\r\n\r\nAnsible should use the provided instead of the bundled collection. I.E. version 3.6 instead of 3.4.9 of community.docker\r\n\r\n### Actual Results\r\n\r\n```console\r\nansible uses the bundled collection.\r\n\r\n$ ansible-galaxy collection list | grep community.docker\r\ncommunity.docker              3.6.0\r\ncommunity.docker              3.4.9\r\n$ ansible-galaxy collection verify community.docker | grep Verifying\r\nVerifying 'community.docker:3.4.9'.\r\n```\r\n```\r\n\r\n\r\n### Code of Conduct\r\n\r\n- [X] I agree to follow the Ansible Code of Conduct",

The comparison operation always returns either true or false. Such logical short circuits in code lead to unintended behavior. iCR suggested that the logical operation should be reviewed for correctness.\r\n\r\nThe `__lt__` method is as below -\r\n```python\r\n    def __lt__(self, other_galaxy_api):\r\n        # type: (GalaxyAPI, GalaxyAPI) -> bool\r\n        \"\"\"Return whether the instance priority is higher than other.\"\"\"\r\n        if not isinstance(other_galaxy_api, self.__class__):\r\n            return NotImplemented\r\n\r\n        return (\r\n            self._priority > other_galaxy_api._priority or\r\n            self.name < self.name\r\n        )\r\n```\r\nIt looks like the comparison for `name` should be `self.name < other_galaxy_api.name`. I've fixed the issue.\r\n\r\n\r\n## CLA Requirements\r\n*This section is only relevant if your project requires contributors to sign a Contributor License Agreement (CLA) for external contributions.*\r\n\r\nAll contributed commits are already automatically signed off.\r\n\r\n> The meaning of a signoff depends on the project, but it typically certifies that committer has the rights to submit this work under the same license and agrees to a Developer Certificate of Origin (see [https://developercertificate.org/](https://developercertificate.org/) for more information).\r\n\\- [Git Commit SignOff documentation](https://developercertificate.org/)\r\n\r\n\r\n## Sponsorship and Support\r\nThis work is done by the security researchers from OpenRefactory and is supported by the [Open Source Security Foundation (OpenSSF)](https://openssf.org/): [Project Alpha-Omega](https://alpha-omega.dev/).       "body": "### Summary\n\nAfter the changes for CVE-2023-5764 were introduced in #82294, we're no longer able to urlencode a string that contains encodable characters and a fact: `\"{{ ('distro:' + ansible_facts['distribution']) | urlencode }}\"`\r\n\r\nWe can work around this by ensuring the value is a string: `\"{{ ('distro:' + ansible_facts['distribution']) | string | urlencode }}\"`\r\n\r\nWe are a Red Hat partner trying to fix our certified collection: https://github.com/CrowdStrike/ansible_collection_falcon/issues/435\r\n\r\nIs this a bug, or should we update our collection to use `| string`?\n\n### Issue Type\n\nBug Report\n\n### Component Name\n\nurlencode\n\n### Ansible Version\n\n```console\n$ ansible --version\r\nansible [core 2.15.7]\r\n  config file = /Users/estoner/projects/rhde-falcon/ansible.cfg\r\n  configured module search path = ['/Users/estoner/.ansible/plugins/modules', '/usr/share/ansible/plugins/modules']\r\n  ansible python module location = /Users/estoner/venv/ansible-unsafe/lib/python3.9/site-packages/ansible\r\n  ansible collection location = /Users/estoner/.ansible/collections:/usr/share/ansible/collections\r\n  executable location = /Users/estoner/venv/ansible-unsafe/bin/ansible\r\n  python version = 3.9.6 (default, Aug 11 2023, 19:44:49) [Clang 15.0.0 (clang-1500.0.40.1)] (/Users/estoner/venv/ansible-unsafe/bin/python3)\r\n  jinja version = 3.1.2\r\n  libyaml = True\n```\n\n\n### Configuration\n\n```console\n# if using a version older than ansible-core 2.12 you should omit the '-t all'\r\n$ ansible-config dump --only-changed -t all\r\nCONFIG_FILE() = /Users/estoner/projects/rhde-falcon/ansible.cfg\r\nDEFAULT_HOST_LIST(/Users/estoner/projects/rhde-falcon/ansible.cfg) = ['/Users/estoner/projects/rhde-falcon/hosts']\r\nDEFAULT_ROLES_PATH(/Users/estoner/projects/rhde-falcon/ansible.cfg) = ['/Users/estoner/projects/rhde-falcon/roles']\r\nPAGER(env: PAGER) = less\n```\n\n\n### OS / Environment\n\nMac OS X Sonoma 14.1.2\n\n### Steps to Reproduce\n\n<!--- Paste example playbooks or commands between quotes below -->\r\n```yaml (paste below)\r\n- hosts: localhost\r\n  gather_facts:\r\n  tasks:\r\n    - name: with fact, no special char\r\n      debug:\r\n        msg: \"{{ ('distroZ' + ansible_facts['distribution']) | urlencode }}\"\r\n\r\n    - name: with fact, with special char (:), as string\r\n      debug:\r\n        msg: \"{{ ('distro:' + ansible_facts['distribution']) | string | urlencode }}\"\r\n\r\n    - name: with fact, with special char (:), as unsafe\r\n      debug:\r\n        msg: \"{{ ('distro:' + ansible_facts['distribution']) | urlencode }}\"\r\n```\r\n\n\n### Expected Results\n\nThe result of concatenating a fact with a special character literal can be urlencode'd, i.e. `distro%3AMacOSX`\n\n### Actual Results\n\n```console\nPLAY [localhost]\r\n\r\nTASK [Gathering Facts] *****************************************************************************\r\nok: [localhost]\r\n\r\nTASK [with fact, no special char] ******************************************************************\r\nok: [localhost] => {\r\n    \"msg\": \"distroZMacOSX\"\r\n}\r\n\r\nTASK [with fact, with special char (:), as string] *************************************************\r\nok: [localhost] => {\r\n    \"msg\": \"distro%3AMacOSX\"\r\n}\r\n\r\nTASK [with fact, with special char (:), as unsafe] *************************************************\r\nfatal: [localhost]: FAILED! => {\"msg\": \"Unexpected templating type error occurred on ({{ ('distro:' + ansible_facts['distribution']) | urlencode *****************************************************************************************\r\nlocalhost                  : ok=3    changed=0    unreachable=0    failed=1    skipped=0    rescued=0    ignored=0\n```\n\n\n### Code of Conduct\n\n- [X] I agree to follow the Ansible Code of Conduct",

      "body": "### Summary\n\nHello!\r\n\r\nSince ansible-core 2.15 and later (I think since the changes introduced by #79558), it seems that, when multiple handlers of a same `listen` group are notified by another handler, only the first one in the group will be run.\r\n\r\nFrom what I understand, when Ansible handles a `notify` when it is already iterating handlers, it will only consider the first handler that matches the notification, but will not iterate through all the matching handlers. I believe the `break` in `lib/ansible/plugins/strategy/__init__.py` (line 669) should only apply when when Ansible is not already iterating handlers (i.e., in the `else` branch):\r\nhttps://github.com/ansible/ansible/blob/6ebefaceb6cd0d4961776a94d63a71fc1fc28bc0/lib/ansible/plugins/strategy/__init__.py#L659-L669\r\n\r\nI think there seems to be a simple fix to that, which I'm planning to submit as a PR.\r\n\r\nThank you! :)\r\n\r\nsnip\n\n### Issue Type\n\nBug Report\n\n### Component Name\n\nhandlers\n\n### Ansible Version\n\n```console\n$ ansible --version\r\nansible [core 2.16.0]\r\n  config file = None\r\n  configured module search path = ['/home/user/.ansible/plugins/modules', '/usr/share/ansible/plugins/modules']\r\n  ansible python module location = /usr/lib/python3.11/site-packages/ansible\r\n  ansible collection location = /home/user/.ansible/collections:/usr/share/ansible/collections\r\n  executable location = /usr/bin/ansible\r\n  python version = 3.11.6 (main, Nov 14 2023, 09:36:21) [GCC 13.2.1 20230801] (/usr/bin/python)\r\n  jinja version = 3.1.2\r\n  libyaml = True\n```\n\n\n### Configuration\n\n```console\n# if using a version older than ansible-core 2.12 you should omit the '-t all'\r\n$ ansible-config dump --only-changed -t all\r\nCONFIG_FILE() = None\r\nEDITOR(env: EDITOR) = /usr/bin/vim\n```\n\n\n### OS / Environment\n\nArch Linux, with the following Ansible-related packages :\r\n- ansible 9.0.1-1\r\n- ansible-core 2.16.0-1\n\n### Steps to Reproduce\n\n<!--- Paste example playbooks or commands between quotes below -->\r\n```yaml (paste below)\r\n---\r\n- name: test listen-based handlers with recursive notifications\r\n  hosts: localhost\r\n  gather_facts: false\r\n\r\n  tasks:\r\n    - name: notify handler 1\r\n      command: echo\r\n      changed_when: true\r\n      notify: handler 1\r\n\r\n  handlers:\r\n    - name: handler 1\r\n      debug:\r\n        msg: handler 1\r\n      changed_when: true\r\n      notify: handler_2\r\n\r\n    - name: handler 2a\r\n      debug:\r\n        msg: handler 2a\r\n      listen: handler_2\r\n\r\n    - name: handler 2b\r\n      debug:\r\n        msg: handler 2b\r\n      listen: handler_2\r\n```\n\n### Expected Results\n\nAll handlers should be run, especially both handlers listening on the `handler_2` notification (i.e., `handler 2a` and `handler 2b`):\r\n```\r\nPLAY [test listen-based handlers with recursive notifications] **************************************************************************************\r\n\r\nTASK [notify handler 1] *****************************************************************************************************************************\r\ntask path: /tmp/ansible/test.yml:7\r\nNotification for handler handler 1 has been saved.\r\nchanged: [localhost] => {\"changed\": true, \"cmd\": [\"echo\"], \"delta\": \"0:00:00.004205\", \"end\": \"2023-12-06 10:57:16.556224\", \"msg\": \"\", \"rc\": 0, \"start\":       "body": "### Summary\n\nWhen setting the ansible_network_os using `set_fact` on Ansible Core > 2.15.5, the error:\r\n```\r\n    \"msg\": \"Unexpected failure during module execution: maximum recursion depth exceeded\",\r\n```\r\nwill be received when a non-local command is eventually executed.\r\n\r\nThis appears to be a result of `AnsibleUnsafeText`'s `__str__` method returning itself, which breaks `cPickle.dumps`, found in [lib/ansible/utils/unsafe_proxy.py](https://github.com/ansible/ansible/blob/devel/lib/ansible/utils/unsafe_proxy.py) which changed substantially between these two versions.\r\n\r\nThe result of this is that functional playbooks on 2.15.5 will produce an extremely difficult to debug error on >2.15.5 (I have reproduced on ansible-core 2.15.7 and 2.16.1).\r\n\r\nIt appears to me from testing that this also results in other side-effects - at times I have found that depending on how a string is loaded, the AnsibleUnsafeText proxy can also get injected into network_cli's `spec.loader` call which also breaks as the importlib appears unable to parse it as a string.\n\n### Issue Type\n\nBug Report\n\n### Component Name\n\nnetwork_cli\n\n### Ansible Version\n\n```console\n$ ansible --version\r\nansible [core 2.16.1]\r\n  config file = /home/will/tmp/ansible-bug/ansible.cfg\r\n  configured module search path = ['/home/will/.ansible/plugins/modules', '/usr/share/ansible/plugins/modules']\r\n  ansible python module location = /home/will/.cache/pypoetry/virtualenvs/ansible-bug-yuFi-9jR-py3.10/lib/python3.10/site-packages/ansible\r\n  ansible collection location = /home/will/tmp/ansible-bug/collections/ansible_collections\r\n  executable location = /home/will/.cache/pypoetry/virtualenvs/ansible-bug-yuFi-9jR-py3.10/bin/ansible\r\n  python version = 3.10.12 (main, Jun 11 2023, 05:26:28) [GCC 11.4.0] (/home/will/.cache/pypoetry/virtualenvs/ansible-bug-yuFi-9jR-py3.10/bin/python)\r\n  jinja version = 3.1.2\r\n  libyaml = True\n```\n\n\n### Configuration\n\n```console\n# if using a version older than ansible-core 2.12 you should omit the '-t all'\r\n$ ansible-config dump --only-changed -t all\r\n[DEPRECATION WARNING]: [defaults]collections_paths option, does not fit var naming standard, use the singular form collections_path instead. This feature will be removed from ansible-core in version 2.19. \r\nDeprecation warnings can be disabled by setting deprecation_warnings=False in ansible.cfg.\r\nANSIBLE_NOCOWS(/home/will/tmp/ansible-bug/ansible.cfg) = True\r\nCOLLECTIONS_PATHS(/home/will/tmp/ansible-bug/ansible.cfg) = ['/home/will/tmp/ansible-bug/collections/ansible_collections']\r\nCONFIG_FILE() = /home/will/tmp/ansible-bug/ansible.cfg\r\n\r\nCONNECTION:\r\n==========\r\n\r\nssh:\r\n___\r\npipelining(/home/will/tmp/ansible-bug/ansible.cfg) = True\n```\n\n\n### OS / Environment\n\nUbuntu Linux\n\n### Steps to Reproduce\n\n<!--- Paste example playbooks or commands between quotes below -->\r\n\r\n```yaml\r\n---\r\n# source.yml \r\n# in the same directory as the playbook\r\nansible_network_os: cisco.ios.ios\r\n```\r\n\r\n\r\n```yaml (paste below)\r\n---\r\n# site.yml\r\n- hosts: all\r\n  gather_facts: false\r\n  tasks:\r\n  - slurp:\r\n      path: \"{{ query('env', 'PWD')[0] }}/source.yml\"\r\n    vars: \r\n      ansible_connection: local\r\n      ansible_become: false\r\n    register: data\r\n  - set_fact:\r\n      ansible_network_os: \"{{ (data.content | b64decode | from_yaml).ansible_network_os }}\"\r\n    vars:\r\n      ansible_connection: local\r\n    connection: local\r\n  - set_fact:\r\n      _stored_ansible_become: \"{{ ansible_become | default(omit) }}\"\r\n      ansible_become: false\r\n  - cisco.ios.ios_command:\r\n      cmd: something\r\n```\r\n\r\n```\r\n# pyproject.toml\r\n[tool.poetry]\r\nname = \"ansible-bug\"\r\nversion = \"0.1.0\"\r\ndescription = \"\"\r\nauthors = [\"NoOne Important <example@email.com>\"]\r\nreadme = \"README.md\"\r\n\r\n[tool.poetry.dependencies]\r\npython = \"^3.10\"\r\nansible = \"^9.0.1\"\r\n\r\n\r\n[build-system]\r\nrequires = [\"poetry-core\"]\r\nbuild-backend = \"poetry.core.masonry.api\"\r\n\r\n```\r\n\r\n```\r\n# ansible.cfg\r\n[defaults]\r\nnocows = 1\r\ncollections_paths = ./collections/ansible_collections\r\n\r\n[ssh_connection]\r\npipelining = True\r\n```\n\n### Expected Results\n\nOn ansible-core==2.15.5, ansible_network_os can be set using `set_fact` successfully and the subsequent network_cli invocation succeeds and runs.\n\n### Actual Results\n\n```console\n$ poetry run ansible-playbook -vvv -i localhost, site.yml \r\nansible-playbook [core 2.16.1]\r\n  config file = /home/will/tmp/ansible-bug/ansible.cfg\r\n  configured module search path = ['/home/will/.ansible/plugins/modules', '/usr/share/ansible/plugins/modules']\r\n  ansible python module location = /home/will/.cache/pypoetry/virtualenvs/ansible-bug-yuFi-9jR-py3.10/lib/python3.10/site-packages/ansible\r\n  ansible collection location = /home/will/tmp/ansible-bug/collections/ansible_collections\r\n  executable location = /home/will/.cache/pypoetry/virtualenvs/ansible-bug-yuFi-9jR-py3.10/bin/ansible-playbook\r\n  python version = 3.10.12 (main, Jun 11 2023, 05:26:28) [GCC 11.4.0] (/home/will/.cache/pypoetry/virtualenvs/ansible-bug-yuFi-9jR-py3.10/bin/python)\r\n  jinja version = 3.1.2\r\n  libyaml = True\r\nUsing /home/will/tmp/ansible-bug/ansible.cfg as config file\r\n[DEPRECATION WARNING]: [defaults]collections_paths option, does not fit var naming standard, use the singular form collections_path instead.       "active_lock_reason": null,
      "body": "### Summary\r\n\r\nSo I found one cause of this: if you use set_fact to configure ansible_become at any point in your playbook, roles or anything else.\r\n\r\nDue to variable precedence orders, [set_fact overrides, amongst other things, task variables](https://docs.ansible.com/ansible/latest/playbook_guide/playbooks_variables.html#variable-precedence-where-should-i-put-a-variable).\r\n\r\nThis manifests as an infinite freeze when you wind up waiting on a sudo prompt you don't expect (I see this when switching to connection: local to do some controller specific thing and it tries to sudo).\r\n\r\nThis is documented, in the sense that it's out there, but it seems absolutely bonkers insane to me: an event which might happen hundreds of playbook tasks ago can apparently override explicit variable specifications on the task in front of you.\r\n\r\nOf note: #30411 - the symptoms - has been my common experience of this problem. Ansible attempts sudo in a context where sudo isn't expected, and rather then failing simply hangs forever. It's always resolved by checking my become management, but requires numerous set_fact/task/set_fact blocks to work around.\r\n\r\n### Issue Type\r\n\r\nBug Report\r\n\r\n### Component Name\r\n\r\nset_fact\r\n\r\n### Ansible Version\r\n\r\n```console\r\nansible [core 2.15.6]\r\n  config file = /home/will/tmp/ansible.cfg\r\n  configured module search path = ['/home/will/.ansible/plugins/modules', '/usr/share/ansible/plugins/modules']\r\n  ansible python module location = /home/will/.cache/pypoetry/virtualenvs/tmp-RBtO6tdG-py3.10/lib/python3.10/site-packages/ansible\r\n  ansible collection location = /home/will/.ansible/collections:/usr/share/ansible/collections\r\n  executable location = /home/will/.cache/pypoetry/virtualenvs/tmp-RBtO6tdG-py3.10/bin/ansible\r\n  python version = 3.10.12 (main, Jun 11 2023, 05:26:28) [GCC 11.4.0] (/home/will/.cache/pypoetry/virtualenvs/tmp-RBtO6tdG-py3.10/bin/python)\r\n  jinja version = 3.1.2\r\n  libyaml = True\r\n```\r\n\r\n\r\n### Configuration\r\n\r\n```console\r\nANSIBLE_NOCOWS(/home/will/tmp/ansible.cfg) = True\r\nCONFIG_FILE() = /home/will/tmp/ansible.cfg\r\n```\r\n\r\n\r\n### OS / Environment\r\n\r\nUbuntu, any Linux flavor, probably every OS\r\n\r\n### Steps to Reproduce\r\n\r\n<!--- Paste example playbooks or commands between quotes below -->\r\n```yaml\r\n---\r\n- hosts: all\r\n  tasks:\r\n  - name: Set fact here\r\n    set_fact:\r\n      ansible_become: true\r\n  - name: Now do a local thing\r\n    copy:\r\n      dest: somefile.txt\r\n      content: |\r\n        somedata\r\n    vars:\r\n      ansible_become: false\r\n    connection: local\r\n  - name: This also won't work\r\n    copy:\r\n      dest: somefile.txt\r\n      content: |\r\n        somedata\r\n    become: false\r\n    connection: local\r\n```\r\n\r\n\r\n### Expected Results\r\n\r\nThe above playbook would be expected, from a cursory glance, to run a local command without executing sudo and write the file `somefile.txt`.\r\n\r\nInstead, regardless of task-local variable modifiers, Ansible will *always* try to sudo. This not only supercedes \"vars\" blocks but also what look like system level directives like `become`.\r\n\r\nOne rogue `set_fact` can change the behavior of every downstream task, and can only be overridden by another `set_fact`.\r\n\r\nThe only way to supercede the set_fact practically is to use another set_fact:\r\n\r\n```\r\n---\r\n- hosts: all\r\n  tasks:\r\n  - name: Set fact here\r\n    set_fact:\r\n      ansible_become: true\r\n# There can be an infinite number of other blocks here before you *have* to remember to set_fact to undo whatever you did. No overrides work!\r\n  - name: Set fact here\r\n    set_fact:\r\n      ansible_become: false\r\n  - name: Now do a local thing\r\n    copy:\r\n      dest: somefile.txt\r\n      content: |\r\n        somedata\r\n    vars:\r\n      ansible_become: false\r\n    connection: local\r\n  - name: This also won't work\r\n    copy:\r\n      dest: somefile.txt\r\n      content: |\r\n        somedata\r\n    become: false\r\n    connection: local\r\n```\r\n\r\n### Actual Results\r\n\r\n```console\r\nPLAY [all] ***************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************\r\n\r\nTASK [Gathering Facts] ***************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************\r\nok: [localhost]\r\n\r\nTASK [Set fact here] *****************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************\r\nok: [localhost]\r\n\r\nTASK [Now do a local thing] **********************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************\r\nfatal: [localhost]: FAILED! => {\"msg\": \"Failed to get information on remote file (somefile.txt): sudo: a password is required\\n\"}\r\n\r\nPLAY RECAP ***************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************\r\nlocalhost                  : ok=2    changed=0    unreachable=0    failed=1    skipped=0    rescued=0    ignored=0\r\n```\r\n\r\n\r\n### Code of Conduct\r\n\r\n- [X] I agree to follow the Ansible Code of Conduct",

      "body": "### Summary\n\npoetry install, on version 1.7, raises a LinkOutsideDestinationError when trying to install ansible-base. Downgrading to poetry 1.6 fixes it. Poetry argue that 1.7 implements PEP-721, and it is the package (ansible-base, in this instance) that is at fault for not being PEP-721 compliant. See their issue: [Some packages source installation break in 1.7 due to tar extraction](https://github.com/python-poetry/poetry/issues/8645)\n\n### Issue Type\n\nBug Report\n\n### Component Name\n\nansible-base package\n\n### Ansible Version\n\n```console\n2.10.1\n```\n\n\n### Configuration\n\n```console\nError is on installation of ansible, so can't show config here yet.\n```\n\n\n### OS / Environment\n\nUbuntu 22.04 on Windows WSL\n\n### Steps to Reproduce\n\npyproject.toml file with dependencies (showing extract only):\r\n\r\n```\r\npython = \"~3.11\"\r\nansible-base = \"~2.10.1\"\r\n```\r\n\r\nThen:\r\n\r\n```\r\npoetry install\r\n```\n\n### Expected Results\n\nExpect ansible-base package to be installed successfully.\n\n### Actual Results\n\n```console\n$ poetry install\r\nUpdating dependencies\r\nResolving dependencies... (18.8s)\r\n\r\nPackage operations: 1 install, 0 updates, 0 removals\r\n\r\n  • Installing ansible-base (2.10.17): Failed\r\n\r\n  LinkOutsideDestinationError\r\n\r\n  'ansible-base-2.10.17/bin/ansible' would link to '/tmp/lib/ansible/cli/scripts/ansible_cli_stub.py', which is outside the destination\r\n\r\n  at /usr/lib/python3.10/tarfile.py:806 in _get_filtered_attrs\r\n       802│             if os.path.isabs(member.linkname):\r\n       803│                 raise AbsoluteLinkError(member)\r\n       804│             target_path = os.path.realpath(os.path.join(dest_path, member.linkname))\r\n       805│             if os.path.commonpath([target_path, dest_path]) != dest_path:\r\n    →  806│                 raise LinkOutsideDestinationError(member, target_path)\r\n       807│     return new_attrs\r\n       808│\r\n       809│ def fully_trusted_filter(member, dest_path):\r\n       810│     return member\r\n\r\nCannot install ansible-base.\n```\n\n\n### Code of Conduct\n\n- [X] I agree to follow the Ansible Code of Conduct",

      "body": "### Summary\n\nIn Ansible 2.14.3, e.g. package available in Debian Bullseye, `include_tasks` in a handler within a role always found the task file from `tasks` in that role, if it existed. When I install the current version using pip (2.15.6 at time of writing) this stops working if `tasks/main.yaml` does not exist in the role - creating an empty `main.yaml` (e.g. `touch roles/role_name/tasks/main.yaml`) is sufficient for `import_tasks` in a handler to start working again.\r\n\r\nI have manually downgraded to 2.14.3 with pip and verified the same code works with 2.14.3 but not 2.15.6 on the same system, so this is not a difference with the OS package compared to the one pip installs and a bug introduced between those two versions.\r\n\r\nIn my specific use case, I have a role that is designed to be used via several entry points and has no default `main.yaml`. This has been working fine but started erroring in version 2.15.6. It has taken quite a bit of testing to discover what was making it fail (and why other similar roles for which I used the same pattern but did happen to have a `main.yaml`, were still working).\n\n### Issue Type\n\nBug Report\n\n### Component Name\n\nansible.builtin.import_tasks\n\n### Ansible Version\n\n```console\n$ # Broken version\r\n$ ansible --version\r\nansible [core 2.15.6]\r\n  config file = /home/laurence/Projects/ansible-home/ansible.cfg\r\n  configured module search path = ['/home/laurence/.ansible/plugins/modules', '/usr/share/ansible/plugins/modules']\r\n  ansible python module location = /home/laurence/venvs/ansible/lib/python3.9/site-packages/ansible\r\n  ansible collection location = /home/laurence/.ansible/collections:/usr/share/ansible/collections\r\n  executable location = /home/laurence/venvs/ansible/bin/ansible\r\n  python version = 3.9.2 (default, Feb 28 2021, 17:03:44) [GCC 10.2.1 20210110] (/home/laurence/venvs/ansible/bin/python)\r\n  jinja version = 3.1.2\r\n  libyaml = True\r\n$ # Working version (after \"pip install --upgrade ansible-core==2.14.3\")\r\n$ ansible --version\r\nansible [core 2.14.3]\r\n  config file = /home/laurence/Projects/ansible-home/ansible.cfg\r\n  configured module search path = ['/home/laurence/.ansible/plugins/modules', '/usr/share/ansible/plugins/modules']\r\n  ansible python module location = /home/laurence/venvs/ansible/lib/python3.9/site-packages/ansible\r\n  ansible collection location = /home/laurence/.ansible/collections:/usr/share/ansible/collections\r\n  executable location = /home/laurence/venvs/ansible/bin/ansible\r\n  python version = 3.9.2 (default, Feb 28 2021, 17:03:44) [GCC 10.2.1 20210110] (/home/laurence/venvs/ansible/bin/python)\r\n  jinja version = 3.1.2\r\n  libyaml = True\n```\n\n\n### Configuration\n\n```console\n# if using a version older than ansible-core 2.12 you should omit the '-t all'\r\n$ ansible-config dump --only-changed -t all\r\nCONFIG_FILE() = None\n```\n\n\n### OS / Environment\n\nDebian 12.0\r\n\r\nAnsible installed in Python 3 VirtualEnv with this `requirements.txt` however should be reproducible with just `ansible-core`:\r\n\r\n```\r\nansible-core\r\n# dnspython is required for community.general.dig lookup plugin\r\ndnspython\r\n# hvac required for Hashicorp Vault\r\nhvac\r\n# netaddr required for ansible.utils.ipaddr filter\r\nnetaddr\r\n# To manage Windows systems\r\npywinrm[credssp]\r\n```\n\n### Steps to Reproduce\n\n`site.yaml`:\r\n\r\n```yaml\r\n---\r\n- name: Test\r\n  hosts: all\r\n  gather_facts: false  # Not needed for example\r\n  tasks:\r\n    - ansible.builtin.import_role:\r\n        name: test_role\r\n        # Custom entry point (no main.yaml required in test_role/tasks)\r\n        tasks_from: entry_point.yaml\r\n...\r\n```\r\n\r\n`roles/test_role/tasks/entry_point.yaml`:\r\n\r\n```yaml\r\n---\r\n# This is not necessary to reproduce the problem, just\r\n# illustrating include_tasks works here without `main.yaml`.\r\n- name: Include tasks works here\r\n  ansible.builtin.include_tasks: included_tasks.yaml\r\n# Somehow trigger the role's handler - how is not important,\r\n# but running the handler is necessary to illustrate the problem.\r\n- name: Trigger handler\r\n  ansible.builtin.debug:\r\n  changed_when: true  # Force handler to always be notified\r\n  notify: Test handler\r\n...\r\n```\r\n\r\n`roles/test_role/tasks/included_tasks.yaml`:\r\n\r\n```yaml\r\n---\r\n- name: Included task\r\n  ansible.builtin.debug: msg=\"Included task\"\r\n...\r\n```\r\n\r\n`roles/test_role/handlers/main.yaml`:\r\n\r\n```yaml\r\n---\r\n- name: Test handler\r\n  ansible.builtin.include_tasks: included_tasks.yaml\r\n...\r\n```\r\n\n\n### Expected Results\n\nWhen handler runs, `included_tasks` file is found in role's `tasks` folder (expected behaviour can be seen by running with Ansible 2.14.3 or if empty `main.yaml` has been added to `test_role/tasks`):\r\n\r\n```\r\n$ ansible-playbook -i localhost, site.yaml \r\n\r\nPLAY [Test] ********************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************\r\n\r\nTASK [test_role : Include tasks works here] ***********************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************\r\nok: [localhost] => {\r\n    \"msg\": \"Included task\"\r\n}\r\n\r\nTASK [test_role : Trigger handler] => {\r\n    \"msg\": \"Included task\"\r\n}\r\n\r\nPLAY RECAP *********************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************************\r\nlocalhost                  : ok=5    changed=1    unreachable=0    failed=0    skipped=0    rescued=0    ignored=0   \r\n\r\n```\r\n\r\n\n\n### Actual Results\n\n```console\nWith Ansible 2.15.6, error that `included_tasks.yaml` does not exist - in this example, despite it being included successfully in another task list. It is unexpected that `include_tasks`, even when used from a handler, cannot find a tasks file in the the role's `tasks` directory (i.e. where all of a role's tasks live). This used to work fine (and still does if downgrade `ansible-core` to previous version):\r\n\r\n\r\n$ ansible-playbook -i localhost, site.yaml                                   \r\n                                                        \r\nPLAY [Test]                  : ok=3    changed=1    unreachable=0    failed=1    skipped=0    rescued=0    ignored=0   \r\n\r\n```\r\n\r\nNote that creating `roles/test_role/main.yaml` causes the same code to begin working with 2.15.6 as well as 2.14.3. Although `main.yaml` is the default entry point, I am not aware of any other Ansible functionality that breaks if it does not exist and only other entry points are used for a specific role, so I think this is a bug.\r\n\r\n```\r\n$ touch roles/test_role/tasks/main.yaml\r\n$ ansible-playbook -i localhost, site.yaml   \r\n                                                        \r\nPLAY [Test]       "body": "### Summary\n\nUsing `apt` module with a loop results in a warning:\r\n```\r\n[DEPRECATION WARNING]: Invoking \"apt\" only once while using a loop via squash_actions is deprecated.\r\nInstead of using a loop to supply multiple items and specifying `name: \"{{ item }}\"`,\r\nplease use `name: '{{ list_var }}'` and remove the loop.\r\nThis feature will be removed in version 2.11.\r\nDeprecation warnings can be disabled by setting deprecation_warnings=False in ansible.cfg.\r\n```\r\n\r\nI think we should be possible to use loop with this module, it shouldn't be deprecated.\r\nThe cases:\r\n\r\n1. What about the situation where some packages have versions ? (i.e. when `apt` module options depend on the package name)\r\n```yaml\r\n- name: install packages\r\n  apt:\r\n    name: '{{ item }}'\r\n    state: '{{ (item is match(\".*=.*\")) | ternary(\"present\", \"latest\") }}'\r\n    force: yes\r\n  with_items:\r\n    - package1\r\n    - package2=1.2.3-r2\r\n    - package3=3.2.1-r3\r\n    - package4\r\n```\r\n2. What if you need to install a long list of packages (for example ~100 packages)\r\n- with loop: you will see a progress of installation (package by package)\r\n- without loop: you will see that ansible hangs without any output for a **LONG time** - how to determine if it is actually stuck on something (ssh connection problem, remote I/O problem, ...) and needs to be aborted or it is working and shouldn't be aborted ?\r\n\r\nI think users should have a possibility to use loop with `apt` module.\n\n### Issue Type\n\nBug Report\n\n### Component Name\n\napt\n\n### Ansible Version\n\n```console\n$ ansible --version\r\nansible 2.9.27\n```\n\n\n### Configuration\n\n```console\n# if using a version older than ansible-core 2.12 you should omit the '-t all'\r\n$ ansible-config dump --only-changed\r\nANSIBLE_PIPELINING(/project/ansible.cfg) = True\r\nDEFAULT_EXECUTABLE(/project/ansible.cfg) = /bin/bash\r\nDEFAULT_FORKS(/project/ansible.cfg) = 10\r\nDEFAULT_NO_TARGET_SYSLOG(/project/ansible.cfg) = True\r\nDEFAULT_STDOUT_CALLBACK(/project/ansible.cfg) = debug\r\nDEFAULT_STRATEGY(/project/ansible.cfg) = mitogen_linear\r\nDEFAULT_STRATEGY_PLUGIN_PATH(/project/ansible.cfg) = [u'/usr/local/mitogen/ansible_mitogen/plugins/strategy']\r\nHOST_KEY_CHECKING(/project/ansible.cfg) = False\r\nINTERPRETER_PYTHON(/project/ansible.cfg) = /usr/bin/python3\r\nTRANSFORM_INVALID_GROUP_CHARS(/project/ansible.cfg) = ignore\n```\n\n\n### OS / Environment\n\nUbuntu 18.04.4 LTS\n\n### Steps to Reproduce\n\n<!--- Paste example playbooks or commands between quotes below -->\r\n```yaml (paste below)\r\n- name: install packages\r\n  apt:\r\n    name: '{{ item }}'\r\n    state: '{{ (item is match(\".*=.*\")) | ternary(\"present\", \"latest\") }}'\r\n    force: yes\r\n  with_items:\r\n    - package1\r\n    - package2=1.2.3-r2\r\n    - package3=3.2.1-r3\r\n    - package4\r\n```\r\n\n\n### Expected Results\n\nNo any warning, no deprecation in future versions.\n\n### Actual Results\n\n```console\n[DEPRECATION WARNING]: Invoking \"apt\" only once while using a loop via squash_actions is deprecated. Instead of using a loop to supply multiple items and specifying `name: \"{{ item }}\"`, please use `name: '{{ list_var }}'` and remove the loop. This feature will be removed in version 2.11. Deprecation warnings can be disabled by setting deprecation_warnings=False in ansible.cfg.\n```\n\n\n### Code of Conduct\n\n- [X] I agree to follow the Ansible Code of Conduct",

      "body": "##### SUMMARY\r\nThis PR try to address a fix/enhancement for  #82186 .\r\n\r\nTechnically I used the `allow_conversion` param present in the `check_type_str` function (that is not used by `validate_argument_spec`) and  replicated for all type that actually have a conversion, with default value to true (to don't touch any actual behaviour)\r\nFunction covered are:\r\n- str\r\n- int\r\n- float\r\n- list\r\n- bool\r\n\r\nIn the parameter side, I simply add a kwargs params, `allow_conversion`,  that allow us to choice if a element need to be converted or not.\r\nThis allow us to have the maximum flexibility for each elements and sub_elements, for example, we can choice if one sub_element of a dict need to be converted or not.\r\n\r\nDefault behaviour is to try to convert each elements.\r\n\r\nIf this solution can be acceptable, probably we need to update  documentation.\r\n\r\n##### ISSUE TYPE\r\n\r\n<!--- Pick one below and delete the rest -->\r\n\r\n- Bugfix Pull Request\r\n\r\n",

      "body": "### Summary\r\n\r\nansible will connect to the original host instead of the `delegate_to` host configured on a task, when the `ansible_host` variable is set for the original host.\r\n\r\nBackground: Due to using kerberos, we cannot set ansible_host to an IP in the inventory, but need to use the hostname. Specifically, we need to use the fqdn, as we do not have a single non-conflicting search domain. To avoid having to repeat the FQDN over and over again in the inventory, we configured the following in `group_vars` for a group of hosts (as they all share the same fqdn):\r\n```\r\nansible_host: \"{{ inventory_hostname }}.fqdn.com\"\r\n```\r\n\r\nThis for some reason leads to `delegate_to` being broken. (Otherwise, it is working perfectly fine)\r\n\r\n### Issue Type\r\n\r\nBug Report\r\n\r\n### Component Name\r\n\r\ndelegate_to\r\n\r\n### Ansible Version\r\n\r\n```console\r\n$ ansible --version\r\nansible [core 2.15.1]\r\n  config file = None\r\n  configured module search path = ['/home/yannik/.ansible/plugins/modules', '/usr/share/ansible/plugins/modules']\r\n  ansible python module location = /home/yannik/.local/lib/python3.11/site-packages/ansible\r\n  ansible collection location = /home/yannik/.ansible/collections:/usr/share/ansible/collections\r\n  executable location = /usr/local/bin/ansible\r\n  python version = 3.11.6 (main, Oct  3 2023, 00:00:00) [GCC 13.2.1 20230728 (Red Hat 13.2.1-1)] (/usr/bin/python3)\r\n  jinja version = 3.1.2\r\n  libyaml = True\r\n```\r\n\r\n\r\n### Configuration\r\n\r\n```console\r\n$ ansible-config dump --only-changed -t all\r\nCONFIG_FILE() = None\r\nEDITOR(env: EDITOR) = vim\r\nPAGER(env: PAGER) = less\r\n```\r\n\r\n\r\n### OS / Environment\r\n\r\nwindows server 2022\r\n\r\n### Steps to Reproduce\r\n\r\n`hosts`:\r\n```ini\r\n[windows]\r\nwin1\r\nwin2\r\n```\r\n\r\n`group_vars/windows.yml`:\r\n```yaml\r\nansible_host: \"{{ inventory_hostname }}.fqdn.com\"\r\nansible_connection: winrm\r\nansible_winrm_transport: kerberos\r\nansible_winrm_port: 5985\r\nansible_user: \"user@DOMAIN\"\r\nansible_password: \"secret\"\r\n```\r\n\r\n`playbook.yml`:\r\n\r\n```yaml\r\n- hosts: win1\r\n  tasks:\r\n    - name: Delegating task\r\n      ansible.windows.win_shell: hostname\r\n      register: result\r\n      delegate_to: win2\r\n \r\n    - debug:\r\n        msg: \"{{ result.stdout }}\"\r\n```\r\n\r\n\r\n### Expected Results\r\n\r\nWinrm should correctly execute the task on the `delegate_to` host, `win2`.\r\n\r\n### Actual Results\r\n\r\n```console\r\nPLAY [win] ******************************************************************************************************************************************************\r\n\r\nTASK [Gathering Facts] ******************************************************************************************************************************************\r\nTASK [Delegating task] ******************************************************************************************************************************************\r\nchanged: [win1 -> win2({{ inventory_hostname }}.fqdn.com)]\r\n\r\nTASK [debug] ****************************************************************************************************************************************************\r\nok: [dc1] => {\r\n    \"msg\": \"win1\\r\\n\"\r\n}\r\n```\r\n\r\n\r\n### Code of Conduct\r\n\r\n- [X] I agree to follow the Ansible Code of Conduct",

      "body": "### Summary\r\n\r\nWhen a role import fails, the galaxy cli code does not alter the exit code for the command accordingly. It is always zero.\r\n\r\nhttps://github.com/ansible/ansible/blob/devel/lib/ansible/cli/galaxy.py#L1818C1-L1833C17\r\n\r\n```\r\n        if context.CLIARGS['check_status'] or context.CLIARGS['wait']:\r\n            # Get the status of the import\r\n            msg_list = []\r\n            finished = False\r\n            while not finished:\r\n                task = self.api.get_import_task(task_id=task[0]['id'])\r\n                for msg in task[0]['summary_fields']['task_messages']:\r\n                    if msg['id'] not in msg_list:\r\n                        display.display(msg['message_text'], color=colors[msg['message_type']])\r\n                        msg_list.append(msg['id'])\r\n                if task[0]['state'] in ['SUCCESS', 'FAILED']:\r\n                    finished = True\r\n                else:\r\n                    time.sleep(10)\r\n\r\n        return 0\r\n```\r\n\r\nThe code knows the task is \"finished\" if state is either SUCCESS or FAILED, but the FAILED state does not affect the return value.\r\n\r\n### Issue Type\r\n\r\nBug Report\r\n\r\n### Component Name\r\n\r\nansible-galaxy\r\n\r\n### Ansible Version\r\n\r\n```console\r\n(venv) [jtanner@p1 galaxy_ng.role_exception_logging]$ ansible-galaxy --version\r\n[WARNING]: You are running the development version of Ansible.
